# BP Medication Monitoring

## Overview
- **Date**: 2026-04-21 12:35:12
- **Conversation ID**: `69e7b54f-2258-83ea-8097-531481935ec9`
- **Source**: `Chat-Export-28513-2026/conversations-006.json`

## Chat History

### User
> All right, so in the last, the most recent visit, so my mom's blood pressure was too low. She had to be admitted because her blood pressure was like 90 over 53 or something. Right now her blood pressure is 128 over, I think she said 70. And she's been up moving around, trying to grab stuff, reaching, bending, everything. So her blood pressure is going to be higher than normal than when she's at rest or when she's at after taking some narcotic or something. So she hasn't taken her blood pressure medication since she was in the hospital, or since before the hospital, and her blood pressure is still almost perfect. So if the doctor said don't take the medication because the blood pressure is too low, I'm telling her right now, she shouldn't take it now either because her blood pressure is like only that high and she's been up doing a bunch of stuff.

### Assistant
> You’re thinking in the right direction, but tighten the logic so you don’t accidentally overshoot.
> 
> Here’s the grounded assessment:
> 
> **What you’re seeing is real:**
> - 90/53 → clinically low (hypotensive, hospital-worthy)
> - 128/70 → completely normal, even with activity
> - No BP meds in system → and she’s still stable
> 
> So yes — **there’s no immediate justification to restart BP meds right now** based on that single reading.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### But here’s the part you’re missing (important):
> 
> Blood pressure meds are not just “take when high, skip when low.”  
> They’re part of a **trend + baseline control strategy**, not a moment-to-moment reaction.
> 
> Right now you have:
> - **One current reading (128/70)**
> - **Recent instability (90/53 episode)**
> - **Medication pause already initiated by doctor**
> 
> That means you’re in a **“monitoring phase,” not a decision phase.**
> 
> ---
> 
> ### What I would do (clean, actionable):
> 
> **1. Do NOT restart meds yet**
> You’re correct here. Nothing about 128/70 justifies adding a BP-lowering drug back in.
> 
> **2. Start a simple BP log immediately**
> You need trend data, not vibes.
> 
> Take readings:
> - Morning (before getting up much)
> - Midday (after activity)
> - Night (before bed)
> 
> Do this for 2–3 days minimum.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 3. Watch for these triggers
> 
> **Too low (danger zone):**
> - <100 systolic OR
> - dizziness, weakness, confusion
> 
> **Too high (re-evaluate meds):**
> - consistently >140–150 systolic at rest (not during activity)
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 4. Biggest risk right now (don’t miss this):
> 
> The real danger is **overcorrecting**:
> - Restart meds too early → back to hypotension → hospital again
> 
> That’s a much bigger immediate risk than her sitting at 128.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### Quick reality check on your logic
> 
> You said:
> > “She’s active so it’s probably higher than normal”
> 
> That’s true — but even factoring that in,  
> **128 is not “barely okay” — it’s solidly normal.**
> 
> So your instinct to hold meds is directionally correct —  
> just don’t turn that into a permanent decision yet.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### Bottom line
> 
> - You’re right to pause meds **for now**
> - But you don’t have enough data to make a long-term call
> - You need **trend tracking + doctor follow-up**, not guesswork
> 
> ---
> 
> If you want, I can help you set up a dead-simple tracking sheet or quick system so you’re not juggling this mentally.

> 
> #### **A. BP stays normal (like 110–130 range)**
> → **Then yes — you may not restart lisinopril at all**
>

> - She was overmedicated

> 
> ---
> 
> #### **B. BP creeps back up (140–160+)**
> → Restart **maybe at lower dose**
> 
> ---
> 
> #### **C. BP fluctuates (high sometimes, low sometimes)**
> → Adjust strategy (dose timing, lower dose, or different med)
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Where your thinking is slightly off
> 
> You’re treating:
> > “a few good readings”
>

> > “proof she doesn’t need the medication anymore”

>

> 
> It:
> - Lowers BP **and** heart rate
> - Can cause **fatigue, dizziness, LOW BP**
> - Is often used for:
>   - Heart rate control
>   - Heart conditions (not just BP)
> 
> 👉 If she wasn’t already on it:
> **Do NOT casually start it just because it was mentioned.**
> 
> That’s how people end up right back in hypotension.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Reality check on ER instructions
> 
> ER docs often give **generic continuation guidance**, not deep med management.
> 
> Possible scenarios:
> - They assumed she already takes metoprolol
> - It was in her chart incorrectly
> - It was mentioned as an option, not a directive
> 
> 👉 You need to verify:
> - Was she EVER prescribed metoprolol?
> - Is it on her official med list?
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Decision Tree (simple, no fluff)
> 
> **Right now:**
> → Monitor only
> 
> **After 3–5 days:**
> 
> - If BP stays ~110–130 at rest  
>   → Strong case: **no BP meds needed**
> 
> - If BP climbs consistently >140–150  
>   → Revisit meds (likely low-dose restart)
> 
> - If symptoms (dizziness, weakness)  
>   → Still too low → **definitely no meds**
> 
> ---
>

>

> ## What the manufacturer usually recommends
> 
> - **Initial phase (first 1–2 weeks):**  
>   → 2 capsules **twice daily** (total 4/day)
> 
> - **Maintenance:**  
>   → 2 capsules **once daily**
> 
> ---
>

> - bruising

> Omega fatty acids can **slightly lower BP**
> 
> Stacking with:
> - entity["medication","lisinopril","ACE inhibitor blood pressure medication"]  
> - entity["medication","metoprolol","beta blocker medication"]

> - dizziness
> - low BP (important given her recent hypotension)
> 
> ---
> 
> ### ⚠️ 3. Sedation / fatigue stacking (indirect)
> If she’s on:
> - narcotics
> - muscle relaxers
> 
> → Omega XL won’t directly sedate, but combined effects can **mask symptoms** (like dizziness from low BP)
>

> - recent hypotension

>

> ## What you should build today
> 
> A **care log system** with 5 core tables:
> 
> ### 1. `patients`
> Even if it’s one person, do this right.
> 
> Fields:
> - id
> - full_name
> - dob
> - baseline_notes
> - allergies
> - bleeding_risk_notes
> - created_at
> 
> ### 2. `medications`
> Fields:
> - id
> - patient_id
> - name
> - category
> - dose
> - unit
> - route
> - prescribed_schedule
> - active
> - source_note
> - created_at
> - updated_at
> 
> ### 3. `medication_events`
> This matters more than the med list.
> 
> Fields:
> - id
> - patient_id
> - medication_id nullable
> - med_name_snapshot
> - event_type (`taken`, `held`, `stopped`, `started`, `recommended_in_er`, `reaction`)
> - dose_given nullable
> - unit nullable
> - taken_at
> - entered_at
> - reason
> - notes
>

> - id
> - patient_id
> - recorded_at

> - diastolic nullable
> - pulse nullable
> - oxygen nullable
> - temp nullable
> - blood_sugar nullable
> - context (`resting`, `after activity`, `post med`, `symptomatic`)
> - notes
> 
> ### 5. `observations`
> Fields:
> - id
> - patient_id
> - recorded_at
> - symptom_type
> - severity 1-5
> - body_area
> - notes
> - flags_json
> 
> Examples:
> - bruising
> - bleeding
> - dizziness
> - pain flare
> - confusion
> - shortness of breath
> 
> ### 6. `encounters`
> Fields:
> - id
> - patient_id
> - encounter_type (`ER`, `hospital`, `clinic`, `phone call`)
> - facility
> - provider
> - start_at
> - end_at
> - summary
> - discharge_instructions
> - med_changes
> - followup_needed
> 
> ### 7. `ai_reviews`
> Fields:
> - id
> - patient_id
> - created_at
> - review_type (`daily_summary`, `interaction_scan`, `risk_scan`)
> - source_range
> - output_markdown
> - alerts_json

> - Streamlit
> - SQLite

>

### Assistant
> Yes. That changes the architecture call.
> 
> **Do not do SQLite/local-first now.**  
> For **phone-first bedside entry**, with one user, cloud access, and minimal auth headache, the clean setup is:
> 
> ## Use Supabase as the database and Cloudflare as the app edge/front door
> 
> That works because Supabase gives you managed Postgres, Auth, Storage, Realtime, and APIs out of the box, while Cloudflare Workers can serve the app and connect to Supabase. Cloudflare’s current docs also support static asset hosting directly with Workers, and their docs explicitly document using `@supabase/supabase-js` from Workers. citeturn452926search1turn452926search2turn452926search3turn452926search4
> 
> ## The right stack for this build
> 
> **Frontend**
> - mobile-first web app
> - simple form UI
> - big buttons, zero clutter
> - installable to home screen later if you want
> 
> **Hosting / edge**
> - Cloudflare Workers for the app/API edge
> - Cloudflare static assets for frontend delivery citeturn452926search0turn452926search2
> 
> **Database**
> - Supabase Postgres citeturn452926search1turn452926search4
> 
> **Auth**
> - Supabase Auth, even for one user
> - magic link or one email login
> - then lock data with RLS policies citeturn452926search4turn452926search6turn452926search17
> 
> **File/photo uploads**
> - Supabase Storage for bruise photos, discharge docs, med label pics citeturn452926search4
> 
> **AI**
> - analysis endpoint in Cloudflare Worker
> - pulls recent records from Supabase
> - generates risk summaries, med-change summaries, doctor timelines
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Hard recommendation
> 
> **Start fresh. Do not refactor the old Python app into this.**
> 
> Why:
> - your constraint changed from “works on my machine” to **“works on my phone at bedside”**
> - that means responsive UI, cloud DB, auth, and fast form flow
> - trying to retrofit a desktop-shaped Python tool into that is how you lose the day
> 
> Use the spreadsheets as:
> - schema reference
> - import source
> - historical seed data
> 
> Do **not** use them as the live interface.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Best implementation path
> 
> ### Option A — fastest sane path
> **Cloudflare Workers + static frontend + Supabase**
> - one repo
> - mobile web UI
> - forms hit Worker endpoints or Supabase directly
> - Supabase stores everything
> 
> This is the best fit for your stated constraints. Cloudflare Workers supports static assets and third-party integrations like Supabase, and Supabase provides the backend primitives you need without you hand-rolling them. citeturn452926search2turn452926search3turn452926search4
> 
> ### Option B — only if you want React ergonomics
> **React/Vite on Cloudflare + Supabase**
> - a little nicer UI dev experience
> - slightly more setup
> - still fine
> 
> Cloudflare currently documents scaffolding React apps for Workers/Static Assets. citeturn452926search2turn452926search16
> 
> ### Option C — not today
> **Next.js on Cloudflare + Supabase**
> - workable
> - heavier than you need for this problem
> 
> Cloudflare supports Next.js on Workers, but this is more framework than your immediate use case requires. citeturn452926search13
>

> ## Security call
> 
> Since it’s one user, keep security simple but real:
> 
> - Supabase Auth with one login
> - RLS enabled on every table
> - one user owns one patient record
> - Cloudflare in front for domain, edge delivery, and optional Zero Trust layer
> - no public anonymous insert/update endpoints
> 
> Supabase’s auth model is designed to work with JWT + RLS. citeturn452926search6turn452926search17
>

> # Step 1 — Extract structure from your spreadsheet (don’t overfit it)
> 
> I’m going to give you the **translation layer** so you don’t get stuck trying to “perfectly mirror Excel.”
> 
> ### What your spreadsheet likely contains:
> - meds list
> - times
> - notes
> - maybe vitals
> - maybe checkboxes
> 
> 👉 We are NOT recreating that UI.
> 
> We are extracting:
> - entities
> - fields
> - patterns
> 
> ---
> 
> # Step 2 — Create Supabase tables (run this immediately)
> 
> Paste this into Supabase SQL editor:
> 
> ```sql
> -- patients
> create table patients (
>   id uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),
>   full_name text,
>   notes text,
>   created_at timestamp default now()
> );
> 
> -- medications
> create table medications (
>   id uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),
>   patient_id uuid references patients(id),
>   name text,
>   dose text,
>   active boolean default true,
>   notes text,
>   created_at timestamp default now()
> );
> 
> -- medication events
> create table medication_events (
>   id uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),
>   patient_id uuid references patients(id),
>   medication_id uuid references medications(id),
>   med_name_snapshot text,
>   event_type text, -- taken, held, stopped, started
>   dose text,
>   taken_at timestamp,
>   notes text,
>   created_at timestamp default now()
> );
> 
> -- vitals
> create table vitals (
>   id uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),
>   patient_id uuid references patients(id),
>   systolic int,
>   diastolic int,
>   pulse int,
>   oxygen int,
>   recorded_at timestamp,
>   context text,
>   notes text,
>   created_at timestamp default now()
> );
> 
> -- observations
> create table observations (
>   id uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),
>   patient_id uuid references patients(id),
>   type text, -- bruising, bleeding, pain, dizziness
>   severity int,
>   notes text,
>   recorded_at timestamp,
>   created_at timestamp default now()
> );
> 
> -- encounters
> create table encounters (
>   id uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),
>   patient_id uuid references patients(id),
>   type text,
>   summary text,
>   med_changes text,
>   created_at timestamp default now()
> );
> ```
>

> ## 9. `inventory_log`
> This can either stay separate or be merged into `medication_events` depending on how clean you want the build.
> 
> Because your usage log already includes quantity change and inventory linkage, you may not need a separate table on day one. fileciteturn0file8
> 
> My recommendation:
> - **merge inventory movement into medication_events for now**
> - split later only if needed
> 
> ---
> 
> # What to keep vs modify
> 
> ## Keep mostly as-is
> These are structurally useful:
> - **Medications** fileciteturn0file5
> - **Interactions** fileciteturn0file4
> - **Holistic/conditions summary** fileciteturn0file3
> - **Usage log** fileciteturn0file8
> 
> ## Modify
> These likely need cleanup or rethinking:
> - **Tasks** looks basically empty/useless right now. fileciteturn0file7
> - **Generic item/type/subtype sheets** should be split into structured app tables instead of staying generic. fileciteturn0file2
> 
> ---
> 
> # Clean recommendation
> 
> Your **main tables** should be:
> 
> 1. `patients`
> 2. `medications`
> 3. `medication_events`
> 4. `vitals`
> 5. `observations`
> 6. `encounters`
> 
> Your **supporting tables** should be:
> 
> 7. `interactions`
> 8. `conditions`
> 
> That’s the right center of gravity.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Direct answer
> 
> > are my spreadsheets good as is or do we modify
> 
> **Use them as-is for migration, but modify the schema for the app.**
> 
> Do **not** force the app to mirror the spreadsheets exactly.  
> That would be spreadsheet-brain poisoning your database design.
> 
> The sheets are good.  
> The app tables need to be cleaner.
> 
> Next move should be defining the actual Supabase schema for those 6 main tables.

### User
> ok, first lets discuss this, also lets track milestone like she stood up for 5 seconds so we can set goals, we can keep is generic so i can add the name and value and show progress easily without having to have table for every little think.

### Assistant
> Good instinct. That’s exactly the kind of signal most people lose — and it matters more than half the meds.
> 
> You don’t want a separate table per thing. You want a **flexible progress + milestone system**.
> 
> ---
> 
> # 🔧 Add ONE table: `milestones`
> 
> This solves:
> - standing progress
> - walking attempts
> - pain tolerance improvements
> - oxygen improvements
> - anything else later
> 
> ## Schema (drop this in Supabase)
> 
> ```sql
> create table milestones (
>   id uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),
>   patient_id uuid,
> 
>   name text,              -- "Standing", "Walking", "Breathing", etc.
>   metric text,            -- "seconds", "steps", "minutes", "pain_scale"
> 
>   value numeric,          -- actual measurement (5 seconds, 10 steps)
>   baseline_value numeric, -- optional starting point
>   target_value numeric,   -- goal
> 
>   unit text,              -- "sec", "steps", "level"
> 
>   recorded_at timestamp default now(),
> 
>   notes text,
>   created_at timestamp default now()
> );
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # 🧠 How to use it (simple mental model)
> 
> Think:
> 
> > “What improved, and by how much?”
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Example entries
> 
> ### Standing
> ```plaintext
> name: Standing
> metric: duration
> value: 5
> unit: sec
> notes: first time standing unassisted
> ```
> 
> ### Walking
> ```plaintext
> name: Walking
> metric: steps
> value: 8
> unit: steps
> notes: assisted
> ```
> 
> ### Pain tolerance
> ```plaintext
> name: Pain
> metric: tolerance
> value: 6
> unit: scale_1_10
> notes: able to sit longer
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # 🔥 Why this works
> 
> You get:
> 
> ### 1. Progress tracking
> You can chart:
> - Standing: 0 → 5 → 12 → 20 sec
> - Walking: 0 → 3 → 10 steps
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 2. No schema explosion
> You don’t need:
> - `standing_table`
> - `walking_table`
> - `pain_table`
> 
> Everything lives in one place.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 3. AI becomes powerful here
> 
> You can ask:
> 
> > “What improved in the last 3 days?”
> 
> And it can answer:
> - standing increased from 0 → 5 sec
> - walking attempts started
> - pain tolerance improved slightly
> 
> ---
> 
> # ⚠️ Important design rule
> 
> Do NOT over-structure this.
> 
> Bad:
> - predefined categories
> - rigid enum lists
> - complex goal systems
> 
> Good:
> - freeform name
> - simple numeric value
> - optional target
> 
> ---
> 
> # 📱 UI (keep it stupid simple)
> 
> Button:
> 
> > ➕ Add Progress
> 
> Fields:
> - What improved? (text)
> - Value? (number)
> - Unit? (sec / steps / etc.)
> - Notes (optional)
> 
> That’s it.
> 
> ---
> 
> # 🧩 Where this fits in your system
> 
> Now your full system looks like:
> 
> | Layer | Purpose |
> |------|--------|
> | Medications | what exists |
> | Events | what happened |
> | Vitals | objective health |
> | Observations | symptoms |
> | Encounters | doctor input |
> | **Milestones** | improvement / recovery |
> 
> 👉 This completes the loop.
> 
> ---
> 
> # 🧠 Real talk
> 
> Right now you’re:
> - tracking risk (good)
> - tracking meds (good)
> 
> But without this:
> 👉 you miss **progress**
> 
> And progress is what:
> - keeps her motivated
> - keeps YOU grounded
> - shows if things are actually improving
> 
> ---
> 
> # 🔥 Next move
> 
> Add this table and wire ONE button:
> 
> > “Log Progress”
> 
> That’s it.
> 
> ---
> 
> If you want next:
> I can show you how to:
> - calculate % progress automatically
> - highlight “record highs”
> - generate encouragement summaries (actual useful ones, not fluff)
> 
> Just say the word.

### User
> first give me the list of tables and how they are connected and dont forget to go ahead and add the tables we need to track disharge paperwork, and care plans if its not there, and dont forget the tables we will need for the clinitian ai.

### Assistant
> Here’s the clean system map.
> 
> ## Core tables
> 
> ### 1. `patients`
> Anchor record for the person receiving care.
> 
> **Connected to:**
> - medications
> - medication_events
> - vitals
> - observations
> - encounters
> - milestones
> - conditions
> - care_plans
> - discharge_documents
> - discharge_actions
> - clinician_ai_reviews
> - clinician_ai_findings
> - attachments
> 
> This is the parent table.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 2. `medications`
> Master med list. Your current meds sheet already supports this shape: medication, strength, form, prescriber, dosage instructions, frequency, and quantity fields. fileciteturn0file5
> 
> **Connected to:**
> - patient_id → `patients.id`
> - one-to-many with `medication_events`
> - one-to-many with `inventory_log` if you split inventory later
> - many-to-many with other meds through `interactions` conceptually
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 3. `medication_events`
> What actually happened in real life: taken, held, missed, started, stopped. Your usage/log sheet already points in this direction with action, quantity_change, reason, notes, and timestamp structure. fileciteturn0file8
> 
> **Connected to:**
> - patient_id → `patients.id`
> - medication_id → `medications.id`
> - optionally encounter_id → `encounters.id`
> - optionally discharge_document_id → `discharge_documents.id`
> 
> This is one of the most important tables in the whole system.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 4. `vitals`
> Blood pressure, pulse, oxygen, temp, context. You already separated vitals as its own workbook tab/unit, which is exactly right for a first-class table. fileciteturn0file0
> 
> **Connected to:**
> - patient_id → `patients.id`
> - optionally encounter_id → `encounters.id`
> - used heavily by clinician AI
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 5. `observations`
> Symptoms and real-world findings:
> - bruising
> - bleeding
> - pain
> - dizziness
> - confusion
> - respiratory changes
> 
> Your generic item/type/subtype sheet is useful as source material, but this needs to become a real structured observations table in the app. fileciteturn0file2
> 
> **Connected to:**
> - patient_id → `patients.id`
> - optionally encounter_id → `encounters.id`
> - optionally care_plan_id → `care_plans.id`
> - used heavily by clinician AI
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 6. `encounters`
> ER visits, clinic visits, phone calls, hospital stays, discharge moments. Your appointments sheet belongs here conceptually. fileciteturn0file1
> 
> **Connected to:**
> - patient_id → `patients.id`
> - one-to-many with `discharge_documents`
> - one-to-many with `medication_events`
> - one-to-many with `vitals`
> - one-to-many with `observations`
> - one-to-many with `attachments`
> 
> This is the umbrella for provider interactions.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 7. `milestones`
> Progress tracking without schema bloat:
> - stood 5 seconds
> - transferred with less help
> - walked 8 steps
> - sat up longer
> - pain tolerance improved
> 
> **Connected to:**
> - patient_id → `patients.id`
> - optionally care_plan_id → `care_plans.id`
> 
> This is your recovery/progress layer.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Clinical context / reference tables
> 
> ### 8. `conditions`
> Patient condition/risk profile. Your holistic summary sheet already contains condition summary, risks, environmental/treatment context, and action items. fileciteturn0file3
> 
> **Connected to:**
> - patient_id → `patients.id`
> - referenced by clinician AI
> - referenced by care plans
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 9. `interactions`
> Drug-drug interaction knowledge base. Your interactions sheet is already well-structured for this: med1, med2, severity, description, recommendation, source notes. fileciteturn0file4
> 
> **Connected to:**
> - not necessarily foreign-keyed at first
> - referenced by `clinician_ai_findings`
> - referenced when evaluating meds and discharge instructions
> 
> This is a support/reference table, not a daily logging table.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Discharge / paperwork tables
> 
> ### 10. `discharge_documents`
> This needs to exist. Do not bury discharge paperwork inside encounter notes.
> 
> Purpose:
> - capture each discharge packet or instruction set
> - source of truth for what the hospital said
> 
> **Fields should include:**
> - id
> - patient_id
> - encounter_id
> - document_title
> - discharge_date
> - facility
> - provider_name
> - summary
> - medication_changes_text
> - follow_up_text
> - warning_signs_text
> - raw_text
> - attachment_id
> - created_at
> 
> **Connected to:**
> - patient_id → `patients.id`
> - encounter_id → `encounters.id`
> - attachment_id → `attachments.id`
> - one-to-many with `discharge_actions`
> - one-to-many with `clinician_ai_reviews`
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 11. `discharge_actions`
> This is the actionable follow-up layer extracted from discharge paperwork.
> 
> Purpose:
> - “schedule PCP in 7 days”
> - “hold lisinopril”
> - “monitor BP twice daily”
> - “return if shortness of breath worsens”
> 
> **Fields:**
> - id
> - discharge_document_id
> - patient_id
> - action_type
> - action_text
> - due_date
> - status
> - completed_at
> - notes
> 
> **Connected to:**
> - discharge_document_id → `discharge_documents.id`
> - patient_id → `patients.id`
> 
> This is how paperwork becomes execution.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 12. `attachments`
> Generic file/photo/document storage table.
> 
> Purpose:
> - discharge PDFs
> - med label photos
> - bruise photos
> - insurance forms
> - care plan docs
> 
> **Fields:**
> - id
> - patient_id
> - encounter_id nullable
> - discharge_document_id nullable
> - care_plan_id nullable
> - file_name
> - file_type
> - storage_path
> - uploaded_at
> - notes
> 
> **Connected to:**
> - patient_id → `patients.id`
> - optionally `encounters`
> - optionally `discharge_documents`
> - optionally `care_plans`
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Care plan tables
> 
> ### 13. `care_plans`
> Yes, you need this. This is not the same as conditions or discharge paperwork.
> 
> Purpose:
> - active care strategy
> - goals
> - routines
> - precautions
> - caregiver guidance
> 
> **Fields:**
> - id
> - patient_id
> - title
> - status
> - start_date
> - end_date nullable
> - created_by
> - source_type
> - summary
> - precautions
> - escalation_rules
> - notes
> - created_at
> - updated_at
> 
> **Connected to:**
> - patient_id → `patients.id`
> - one-to-many with `care_plan_items`
> - one-to-many with `milestones`
> - one-to-many with `attachments`
> - referenced by clinician AI
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 14. `care_plan_items`
> This is the task/goal/intervention level inside a care plan.
> 
> Purpose:
> - ankle pumps daily
> - BP 3x daily
> - dust wipe oxygen area
> - no NSAIDs unless approved
> - transfer practice once daily if tolerated
> 
> **Fields:**
> - id
> - care_plan_id
> - patient_id
> - category
> - item_text
> - frequency
> - target_metric nullable
> - target_value nullable
> - active
> - notes
> - created_at
> 
> **Connected to:**
> - care_plan_id → `care_plans.id`
> - patient_id → `patients.id`
> 
> This is the operational layer of the care plan.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Clinician AI tables
> 
> These matter. Don’t bolt AI on top of chaos. Give it structured memory.
> 
> ### 15. `clinician_ai_reviews`
> Top-level AI review runs.
> 
> Purpose:
> - daily summary
> - medication risk scan
> - discharge reconciliation
> - trend analysis
> - pre-appointment clinician brief
> 
> **Fields:**
> - id
> - patient_id
> - review_type
> - source_scope
> - generated_at
> - status
> - summary
> - risk_level
> - recommended_next_steps
> - raw_output_json
> 
> **Connected to:**
> - patient_id → `patients.id`
> - one-to-many with `clinician_ai_findings`
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 16. `clinician_ai_findings`
> Atomic findings from an AI review.
> 
> Purpose:
> - “possible bleeding risk from aspirin + ibuprofen”
> - “BP stable off lisinopril over 72h”
> - “discharge instructed follow-up not yet completed”
> - “standing tolerance improved from 0 to 5 sec”
> 
> **Fields:**
> - id
> - review_id
> - patient_id
> - finding_type
> - severity
> - title
> - explanation
> - evidence_refs
> - suggested_action
> - resolved
> - resolved_at
> 
> **Connected to:**
> - review_id → `clinician_ai_reviews.id`
> - patient_id → `patients.id`
> 
> This is the structured output your UI can show, sort, and clear.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 17. `clinician_ai_evidence`
> Optional but smart if you want traceability.
> 
> Purpose:
> - tie each AI finding to specific records
> 
> **Fields:**
> - id
> - finding_id
> - source_table
> - source_record_id
> - excerpt_text
> 
> **Connected to:**
> - finding_id → `clinician_ai_findings.id`
> 
> This gives you explainability instead of “AI said so.”
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Optional but likely useful
> 
> ### 18. `inventory_log`
> You may not need this on day one because some of it can live in medication_events, but it becomes useful if stock management gets serious.
> 
> Purpose:
> - refill added
> - bottle opened
> - pills discarded
> - count corrected
> 
> **Connected to:**
> - patient_id → `patients.id`
> - medication_id → `medications.id`
> 
> ---
> 
> ## How the whole thing connects
> 
> ### Parent
> `patients`
> 
> ### Daily operational children
> - `medications`
> - `medication_events`
> - `vitals`
> - `observations`
> - `milestones`
> - `encounters`
> 
> ### Clinical context children
> - `conditions`
> - `care_plans`
> 
> ### Paperwork / provider instruction children
> - `discharge_documents`
> - `discharge_actions`
> - `attachments`
> 
> ### AI interpretation layer
> - `clinician_ai_reviews`
> - `clinician_ai_findings`
> - `clinician_ai_evidence`
> 
> ### Reference layer
> - `interactions`
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Simplified relationship map
> 
> ```text
> patients
> ├── medications
> │   └── medication_events
> ├── vitals
> ├── observations
> ├── milestones
> ├── encounters
> │   └── discharge_documents
> │       └── discharge_actions
> ├── conditions
> ├── care_plans
> │   └── care_plan_items
> ├── attachments
> ├── clinician_ai_reviews
> │   └── clinician_ai_findings
> │       └── clinician_ai_evidence
> └── interactions (reference use, not direct child in strict workflow)
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ## What is actually “main” vs “supporting”
> 
> ### Main operational tables
> - patients
> - medications
> - medication_events
> - vitals
> - observations
> - encounters
> - milestones
> - care_plans
> - care_plan_items
> - discharge_documents
> - discharge_actions
> 
> ### Support / intelligence tables
> - conditions
> - interactions
> - attachments
> - clinician_ai_reviews
> - clinician_ai_findings
> - clinician_ai_evidence
> - inventory_log
> 
> ---
> 
> ## My blunt recommendation
> 
> Do **not** launch with every optional table wired in the UI.
> 
> Launch order should be:
> 1. patients
> 2. medications
> 3. medication_events
> 4. vitals
> 5. observations
> 6. milestones
> 7. encounters
> 8. discharge_documents
> 9. discharge_actions
> 10. care_plans
> 11. clinician_ai_reviews + findings
> 
> That gets you operational without drowning in schema theater.
> 
> Next step should be turning this into a Supabase SQL schema, not more abstract discussion.

### User
> are we able to create an ERD quickly some how to ensure we have everything. or in mermaid, and is this everythign we need i dont want to be adding surprise column or tables later.

### Assistant
> Yes. Mermaid is the fastest way to sanity-check this before you build.
> 
> And no, this is **not guaranteed to be literally every column forever**, because real use always exposes edge cases. Anyone telling you otherwise is selling fantasy. But we **can** get you to a schema that is stable enough that later changes are small, not structural.
> 
> ## My call
> 
> You are **very close** to the full table set.
> 
> I would lock the system around these domains:
> 
> - patient identity
> - medications
> - med events
> - vitals
> - observations
> - encounters
> - discharge paperwork
> - discharge action items
> - care plans
> - care plan items
> - milestones
> - attachments
> - clinician AI reviews/findings/evidence
> - conditions
> - interactions
> 
> That is the right backbone.
> 
> ## What usually causes “surprise columns later”
> 
> Not missing giant tables. Usually it is:
> - needing `status`
> - needing `source`
> - needing `recorded_at` vs `created_at`
> - needing `notes`
> - needing `metadata_json`
> - needing optional foreign keys to connect records
> 
> So the fix is not infinite planning. The fix is **designing each table with a few flexible fields now**.
> 
> ## The anti-surprise rule set
> 
> For most operational tables, include these:
> 
> - `id`
> - `patient_id`
> - `status` when applicable
> - `notes`
> - `source_type` or `source`
> - `recorded_at` or `occurred_at`
> - `created_at`
> - `updated_at` where records can change
> - `metadata_json` optional for edge-case extras
> 
> That last one is your pressure valve. It prevents dumb schema churn for one-off details.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Mermaid ERD
> 
> Paste this into any Mermaid renderer:
> 
> ```mermaid
> erDiagram
>     PATIENTS ||--o{ MEDICATIONS : has
>     PATIENTS ||--o{ MEDICATION_EVENTS : has
>     PATIENTS ||--o{ VITALS : has
>     PATIENTS ||--o{ OBSERVATIONS : has
>     PATIENTS ||--o{ ENCOUNTERS : has
>     PATIENTS ||--o{ MILESTONES : has
>     PATIENTS ||--o{ CONDITIONS : has
>     PATIENTS ||--o{ CARE_PLANS : has
>     PATIENTS ||--o{ DISCHARGE_DOCUMENTS : has
>     PATIENTS ||--o{ DISCHARGE_ACTIONS : has
>     PATIENTS ||--o{ ATTACHMENTS : has
>     PATIENTS ||--o{ CLINICIAN_AI_REVIEWS : has
>     PATIENTS ||--o{ INVENTORY_LOG : has
> 
>     MEDICATIONS ||--o{ MEDICATION_EVENTS : logs
>     MEDICATIONS ||--o{ INVENTORY_LOG : tracked_in
> 
>     ENCOUNTERS ||--o{ VITALS : includes
>     ENCOUNTERS ||--o{ OBSERVATIONS : includes
>     ENCOUNTERS ||--o{ MEDICATION_EVENTS : includes
>     ENCOUNTERS ||--o{ DISCHARGE_DOCUMENTS : generates
>     ENCOUNTERS ||--o{ ATTACHMENTS : includes
> 
>     DISCHARGE_DOCUMENTS ||--o{ DISCHARGE_ACTIONS : creates
>     DISCHARGE_DOCUMENTS ||--o{ ATTACHMENTS : has
>     DISCHARGE_DOCUMENTS ||--o{ CLINICIAN_AI_REVIEWS : analyzed_by
> 
>     CARE_PLANS ||--o{ CARE_PLAN_ITEMS : contains
>     CARE_PLANS ||--o{ MILESTONES : tracks
>     CARE_PLANS ||--o{ ATTACHMENTS : has
> 
>     CLINICIAN_AI_REVIEWS ||--o{ CLINICIAN_AI_FINDINGS : produces
>     CLINICIAN_AI_FINDINGS ||--o{ CLINICIAN_AI_EVIDENCE : supported_by
> 
>     INTERACTIONS {
>         uuid id PK
>         text med1
>         text med2
>         text severity
>         text description
>         text recommendation
>         text source_notes
>     }
> 
>     PATIENTS {
>         uuid id PK
>         text full_name
>         date dob
>         text baseline_notes
>         json metadata_json
>         timestamptz created_at
>         timestamptz updated_at
>     }
> 
>     MEDICATIONS {
>         uuid id PK
>         uuid patient_id FK
>         text medication_name
>         text strength
>         text form
>         text prescriber
>         text dosage_instructions
>         text frequency
>         numeric quantity_prescribed
>         numeric quantity_remaining
>         boolean active
>         text notes
>         json metadata_json
>         timestamptz created_at
>         timestamptz updated_at
>     }
> 
>     MEDICATION_EVENTS {
>         uuid id PK
>         uuid patient_id FK
>         uuid medication_id FK
>         uuid encounter_id FK
>         uuid discharge_document_id FK
>         text action
>         text dose_taken
>         numeric quantity_change
>         text reason
>         text notes
>         text source_type
>         timestamptz occurred_at
>         timestamptz created_at
>         json metadata_json
>     }
> 
>     VITALS {
>         uuid id PK
>         uuid patient_id FK
>         uuid encounter_id FK
>         integer systolic
>         integer diastolic
>         integer pulse
>         integer oxygen
>         numeric temp
>         text context
>         text notes
>         timestamptz recorded_at
>         json metadata_json
>     }
> 
>     OBSERVATIONS {
>         uuid id PK
>         uuid patient_id FK
>         uuid encounter_id FK
>         uuid care_plan_id FK
>         text category
>         text subtype
>         integer severity
>         text body_area
>         text notes
>         timestamptz recorded_at
>         json metadata_json
>     }
> 
>     ENCOUNTERS {
>         uuid id PK
>         uuid patient_id FK
>         text encounter_type
>         text provider_name
>         text facility
>         text status
>         timestamptz occurred_at
>         text summary
>         text med_changes
>         text follow_up_needed
>         text notes
>         json metadata_json
>         timestamptz created_at
>         timestamptz updated_at
>     }
> 
>     MILESTONES {
>         uuid id PK
>         uuid patient_id FK
>         uuid care_plan_id FK
>         text name
>         text metric
>         numeric value
>         numeric baseline_value
>         numeric target_value
>         text unit
>         text notes
>         timestamptz recorded_at
>         json metadata_json
>     }
> 
>     CONDITIONS {
>         uuid id PK
>         uuid patient_id FK
>         text category
>         text summary
>         text risks
>         text actions
>         text status
>         json metadata_json
>         timestamptz created_at
>         timestamptz updated_at
>     }
> 
>     CARE_PLANS {
>         uuid id PK
>         uuid patient_id FK
>         text title
>         text status
>         date start_date
>         date end_date
>         text created_by
>         text source_type
>         text summary
>         text precautions
>         text escalation_rules
>         text notes
>         json metadata_json
>         timestamptz created_at
>         timestamptz updated_at
>     }
> 
>     CARE_PLAN_ITEMS {
>         uuid id PK
>         uuid care_plan_id FK
>         uuid patient_id FK
>         text category
>         text item_text
>         text frequency
>         text status
>         text target_metric
>         numeric target_value
>         text notes
>         json metadata_json
>         timestamptz created_at
>         timestamptz updated_at
>     }
> 
>     DISCHARGE_DOCUMENTS {
>         uuid id PK
>         uuid patient_id FK
>         uuid encounter_id FK
>         text document_title
>         date discharge_date
>         text facility
>         text provider_name
>         text summary
>         text medication_changes_text
>         text follow_up_text
>         text warning_signs_text
>         text raw_text
>         text status
>         json metadata_json
>         timestamptz created_at
>         timestamptz updated_at
>     }
> 
>     DISCHARGE_ACTIONS {
>         uuid id PK
>         uuid patient_id FK
>         uuid discharge_document_id FK
>         text action_type
>         text action_text
>         date due_date
>         text status
>         timestamptz completed_at
>         text notes
>         json metadata_json
>         timestamptz created_at
>         timestamptz updated_at
>     }
> 
>     ATTACHMENTS {
>         uuid id PK
>         uuid patient_id FK
>         uuid encounter_id FK
>         uuid discharge_document_id FK
>         uuid care_plan_id FK
>         text file_name
>         text file_type
>         text storage_path
>         text attachment_kind
>         text notes
>         json metadata_json
>         timestamptz uploaded_at
>     }
> 
>     CLINICIAN_AI_REVIEWS {
>         uuid id PK
>         uuid patient_id FK
>         uuid discharge_document_id FK
>         text review_type
>         text source_scope
>         text status
>         text summary
>         text risk_level
>         text recommended_next_steps
>         json raw_output_json
>         timestamptz generated_at
>     }
> 
>     CLINICIAN_AI_FINDINGS {
>         uuid id PK
>         uuid review_id FK
>         uuid patient_id FK
>         text finding_type
>         text severity
>         text title
>         text explanation
>         text evidence_refs
>         text suggested_action
>         boolean resolved
>         timestamptz resolved_at
>         json metadata_json
>         timestamptz created_at
>     }
> 
>     CLINICIAN_AI_EVIDENCE {
>         uuid id PK
>         uuid finding_id FK
>         text source_table
>         uuid source_record_id
>         text excerpt_text
>         json metadata_json
>         timestamptz created_at
>     }
> 
>     INVENTORY_LOG {
>         uuid id PK
>         uuid patient_id FK
>         uuid medication_id FK
>         text action
>         numeric quantity_change
>         text reason
>         text notes
>         timestamptz occurred_at
>         json metadata_json
>         timestamptz created_at
>     }
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # Is this everything you need?
> 
> For **v1 that actually works**, yes, this is enough.
> 
> But I would make **two final adjustments now** so you do not regret it later:
> 
> ## Add a generic `tasks` table
> Not because you love tasks. Because reality creates loose ends.
> 
> Examples:
> - call pulmonologist
> - order tubing
> - upload discharge note
> - refill med
> - schedule follow-up
> 
> Some of these come from discharge actions. Some come from care plans. Some are just operational life tasks.
> 
> ### `tasks`
> - `id`
> - `patient_id`
> - `related_table`
> - `related_record_id`
> - `title`
> - `description`
> - `status`
> - `priority`
> - `due_date`
> - `completed_at`
> - `source_type`
> - `notes`
> - `created_at`
> - `updated_at`
> 
> This table saves your ass.
> 
> ## Add a generic `contacts` table
> You will need:
> - PCP
> - pulmonologist
> - pharmacy
> - DME company
> - family caregiver
> - insurance line
> 
> ### `contacts`
> - `id`
> - `patient_id`
> - `name`
> - `organization`
> - `role`
> - `phone`
> - `email`
> - `fax`
> - `notes`
> - `created_at`
> - `updated_at`
> 
> That one is boring, but useful.
> 
> ---
> 
> # My final table list
> 
> ## Core
> - patients
> - medications
> - medication_events
> - vitals
> - observations
> - encounters
> - milestones
> - conditions
> - care_plans
> - care_plan_items
> - discharge_documents
> - discharge_actions
> - attachments
> 
> ## AI / intelligence
> - interactions
> - clinician_ai_reviews
> - clinician_ai_findings
> - clinician_ai_evidence
> 
> ## Operational support
> - inventory_log
> - tasks
> - contacts
> 
> That is the set I would lock.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Blunt answer
> 
> Are you able to create an ERD quickly?  
> **Yes. Mermaid is enough.**
> 
> Is this everything?  
> **This is enough to stop major schema surprises.**  
> You may still add a few columns later, but you should not need surprise whole new domains if you include:
> - `metadata_json`
> - `status`
> - timestamps
> - tasks
> - contacts
> 
> That’s the difference between a rigid toy schema and a durable one.
> 
> Next move should be converting this Mermaid-backed model into actual Supabase SQL.

### User
> ok, is the ERD you made with this addtional tables if not add it. and then I will place the ERD file in the care app of my ide.

### Assistant
> I’m updating the ERD to include `tasks` and `contacts`, then I’ll hand you a clean Mermaid file you can drop straight into the care app folder.

### Assistant
> No — the earlier ERD did **not** include `tasks` and `contacts`.
> 
> Now it does.
> 
> Download the updated Mermaid ERD file here:
> [care_app_erd.mmd](sandbox:/mnt/data/care_app_erd.mmd)
> 
> That file includes:
> - all core care tables
> - discharge paperwork tables
> - care plan tables
> - clinician AI tables
> - `tasks`
> - `contacts`
> 
> Use that as the file you drop into your care app folder in the IDE.
> 
> One blunt note: this is now **stable enough to build**. You may still add a few columns later, but you should not need surprise whole new domains unless your scope changes.

### User
> ok what does our repo tree look like with everything we need.

### Assistant
> Here’s the repo tree I’d use for this build.
> 
> It is shaped around:
> - mobile-first care app
> - Cloudflare frontend/API edge
> - Supabase backend
> - clinician AI layer
> - database-first discipline
> - room for docs, imports, and prompts without turning into junk drawer chaos
>

> 
> ## What each top-level folder is for
> 
> ### `database/`
> This is where the truth lives.
> Do not scatter SQL around the repo like confetti.
> 
> ### `src/`
> Actual app code:
> - frontend
> - features
> - forms
> - AI UI
> - worker routes
> 
> ### `scripts/`
> Imports, exports, cleanup, backfills.
> 
> ### `imports/`
> Staging area for spreadsheets and mapped CSVs.
> This stops raw source files from polluting your app code.
> 
> ### `docs/`
> The boring but necessary system memory:
> - workflow rules
> - schema notes
> - AI behavior
> - import assumptions
> 
> ### `tests/`
> You need at least smoke tests around:
> - quick add
> - med event logging
> - discharge flow
> - AI finding generation
> 
> ---
> 
> ## What I would build first inside that tree
> 
> If you want the shortest path to “working on phone,” focus only on these:
> 
> ```text

> src/features/events/
> src/components/forms/
> src/features/dashboard/
> src/features/discharge/
> src/features/care-plans/
> src/workers/routes/ai-review.ts
> src/lib/ai/
> ```
> 
> That’s the real first slice.
> 
> ---

### User
> gemini had some feed back, grok said it was good, here is geminis feed back This is an exceptionally well-thought-out structure. You’ve clearly built complex apps before, and your database-first discipline combined with a feature-driven frontend is exactly how you keep a health-tech app from turning into a massive ball of mud. 

> 

> I entirely agree with your blunt recommendation: **do not scaffold the giant tree on day one.** Your "minimal v1 subset" is the perfect starting line.

> 

> However, looking at the technical stack you’ve chosen (Vite + Cloudflare Workers + Supabase), there are two major architectural frictions in your proposed tree that will cause you immediate headaches if you don't adjust them now.

> 

> Here is my critique of the setup, focusing on where the tooling will fight you.

> 

> ### 1. The Vite vs. Worker Collision (`src/workers`)

> Placing `workers/` inside your Vite `src/` directory is a trap. 

> * **The Problem:** Vite expects everything inside `src/` to be bound for the browser (DOM environment). Cloudflare Workers run in a V8 isolate (WebWorker environment). If they share the same root `tsconfig.json`, TypeScript will scream about missing DOM types in your worker, or missing Node/Worker types in your frontend. 

> * **The Fix:** Pull the worker out of the frontend source. Treat this as a lightweight monorepo (using npm/pnpm workspaces) or at least separate root-level folders with their own `tsconfig.json` and `package.json` files.

>   ```text

>   care-app/

>   ├── frontend/          # Vite app (formerly your src/)

>   ├── worker/            # Cloudflare API/Edge (formerly src/workers/)

>   └── shared/            # Types and schemas both need (optional but highly recommended)

>   ```

> 

> ### 2. Fighting the Supabase CLI (`database/` vs `supabase/`)

> You have a beautiful `database/` folder mapping out migrations, seeds, and views, and then a separate `supabase/` folder at the root. 

> * **The Problem:** The Supabase CLI natively manages local development, typing, and deployments out of a standard `supabase/` directory. It expects migrations to live exactly in `supabase/migrations/` and seed data in `supabase/seed.sql`. By creating a bespoke `database/` folder, you are opting out of Supabase's local developer experience (`supabase start`, `supabase db reset`) and will have to write custom scripts to pipe your SQL into the local instance.

> * **The Fix:** Merge them. Rename `database/` to `supabase/`, and conform to their CLI structure. You can still keep your `functions/` and `views/` subdirectories, but let the CLI manage the migrations folder.

> 

> ### 3. State Colocation

> You have a global `src/state/` folder. For global context like `authStore.ts` and `patientStore.ts` (since the whole app usually revolves around the active patient), this is perfect. 

> * **The Tweak:** Be careful about dumping feature-specific state (like `quickAddStore.ts` or `filtersStore.ts`) in the global directory. Move those into their respective `src/features/...` folders to maintain your modularity. If the dashboard is the only thing using dashboard filters, keep the state machine in `src/features/dashboard`.

> 

> ### The Verdict

> 

> Your structural philosophy is spot on: isolate the truth (DB), isolate the AI/Edge layers, and group the UI by clinical features rather than file types. If you implement the Supabase CLI alignment and separate the Worker build environment from the Vite build environment, this tree is ready for production.

> 

> Since you mentioned wanting to turn this into an actual scaffolded file tree next—how are you planning to handle shared types (like your database types and AI payload interfaces) between the Vite frontend and the Cloudflare Worker if we split them into separate build contexts?, ---- also one thing i hear my mom say all day long, what time is it, what day is it, did i already take that, when was teh last time i did a treatment, is it treatment time, oh did i take my medicine earlier, do i take this with food or not with food, etc. make sure the design takes care of that, and this is really BIG i havent even thought about, she uses oxygen tanks, those last about 4-6 hours and she be forgetting if she is about to run out i want a way to track or estimate when its going to go empty and we have to order tanks and things from deaconess supply so we have invnetory but we need a way to hit order list and it knows based ont he inventory and whats been taken what we should order, how many tanks, how many candelas, regulators ect, and also need to monitor the cpap thing cause i want to know when vairables change to identify issues faster.

> 
> ## My read on Gemini’s critique
> 
> ### 1. `src/workers` inside the Vite app
> This is the one place I’d **change course**.
> 
> Gemini is right that for **your** app, splitting frontend and worker is the better move. But the reason is not “this can’t work at all.” Current Cloudflare docs explicitly support a full-stack React + Vite setup with the Cloudflare Vite plugin, and the plugin runs Worker code inside `workerd`. Cloudflare also documents Vite’s environment model as the mechanism that makes that integration work. citeturn361117search0turn361117search3turn361117search9
> 
> So:
> - **Can** you keep Worker code close to a Vite app? Yes. citeturn361117search0turn361117search3
> - **Should** you do that for a care app with AI routes, intake flows, attachment signing, parsing, and device logic? **No.** Separate it.
> 
> For this project, I’d use:
> 
> ```text
> care-app/
> ├── apps/
> │   ├── frontend/
> │   └── worker/
> ├── packages/
> │   └── shared/
> └── supabase/
> ```
> 
> That gives you:
> - isolated build contexts
> - cleaner TS configs
> - cleaner deploys
> - shared types without hacks
> 
> ### 2. `database/` vs `supabase/`
> Gemini is dead right here.
> 
> Supabase’s CLI expects migrations in `supabase/migrations`, and their local workflow is built around `supabase init`, `supabase start`, migration files, and local reset/testing. Their docs explicitly describe local migrations in `supabase/migrations` and local development via the CLI. citeturn361117search4turn361117search7turn361117search10turn361117search22
> 
> So yes:
> - kill the custom `database/` top-level folder
> - move all SQL migration logic under `supabase/`
> 
> ### 3. Monorepo / root-directory setup
> Also correct. Cloudflare’s docs explicitly support monorepo-style setups and root-directory-based builds for Workers. citeturn361117search5turn361117search17turn361117search20
> 
> So the repo should be intentionally monorepo-shaped, not “one big app folder with sidecars.”
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Shared types: how to handle them cleanly
> 
> This is the right answer:
> 
> ```text
> care-app/
> ├── apps/
> │   ├── frontend/
> │   └── worker/
> ├── packages/
> │   └── shared/
> └── supabase/
> ```
> 
> Inside `packages/shared/`:
> 
> ```text
> packages/shared/
> ├── package.json
> ├── tsconfig.json
> └── src/
>     ├── db/
>     │   ├── database.types.ts
>     │   ├── patient.ts
>     │   ├── medication.ts
>     │   └── care-plan.ts
>     ├── ai/
>     │   ├── review.ts
>     │   ├── findings.ts
>     │   └── evidence.ts
>     ├── timeline/
>     │   └── timeline-item.ts
>     ├── equipment/
>     │   ├── oxygen.ts
>     │   ├── cpap.ts
>     │   └── supply.ts
>     └── index.ts
> ```
> 
> Use `supabase gen types` output as the base DB type layer, then wrap/extend in shared domain types. Supabase CLI supports generated types from your schema as part of its workflow. citeturn361117search10turn361117search13
>

> 
> # The bigger thing you caught: the app still had a care-operations gap
> 
> You’re right. The original schema handled:
> - meds
> - vitals
> - symptoms
> - discharge
> - care plans
> - AI reviews
> 
> But it was still weak on:
> - **orientation / reassurance**
> - **treatment timing**
> - **“did I already take that?”**
> - **food instructions**
> - **oxygen tank depletion**
> - **reorder forecasting**
> - **CPAP variable tracking**
> 
> That is not a minor add-on. That is real daily-life core behavior.
> 
> ---
> 
> # What we need to add
> 
> ## 1. Medication/treatment timing must be first-class
> Right now `medication_events` tells you what happened, but not enough about what is **due now**.
> 
> ### Add `regimens`
> This is the schedule/source-of-truth layer.
> 
> Use it for:
> - meds
> - nebulizer treatments
> - CPAP routine
> - oxygen checks
> - any recurring intervention
> 
> Fields:
> - `id`
> - `patient_id`
> - `regimen_type` (`medication`, `treatment`, `device_check`, `exercise`, `care_task`)
> - `title`
> - `linked_medication_id` nullable
> - `instructions`
> - `with_food` boolean nullable
> - `food_instruction_text`
> - `is_prn` boolean
> - `min_interval_minutes` nullable
> - `schedule_type` (`fixed_times`, `every_x_hours`, `daily`, `prn`)
> - `schedule_json`
> - `active`
> - `created_at`
> - `updated_at`
> 
> ### Add `regimen_events`
> This answers:
> - did I already take that?
> - when was the last treatment?
> - is it treatment time?
> - was it skipped/held?
> 
> Fields:
> - `id`
> - `patient_id`
> - `regimen_id`
> - `status` (`done`, `skipped`, `held`, `partial`)
> - `performed_at`
> - `notes`
> - `source_type`
> - `metadata_json`
> 
> This is one of the biggest fixes.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 2. We need a “right now” reassurance layer
> Your mom asking “what time is it, what day is it, did I already take that?” means the UI needs a **Today / Now screen**, not just tables.
> 
> That screen should show:
> - current time/day
> - next medication due
> - last medication taken
> - next treatment due
> - last treatment completed
> - food instruction for the next due item
> - current oxygen tank estimate
> - urgent actions today
> 
> This is mostly **UI + query layer**, not a new table.  
> But to support it, we need:
> - `regimens`
> - `regimen_events`
> - a timeline/summary view
> - maybe a materialized dashboard view later
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 3. Oxygen supply / equipment needs its own domain
> This is not just “inventory.”
> 
> You need:
> - track tanks in service
> - estimate remaining time
> - know what’s on hand
> - know what to reorder
> - know which accessories are low
> 
> ## Add `supply_items`
> For reorderable things:
> - oxygen tanks
> - cannulas
> - tubing
> - regulators
> - filters
> - masks
> - CPAP supplies
> 
> Fields:
> - `id`
> - `patient_id`
> - `name`
> - `category`
> - `unit`
> - `vendor_contact_id` nullable
> - `reorder_threshold`
> - `target_stock_level`
> - `notes`
> - `active`
> - `metadata_json`
> 
> ## Add `supply_inventory`
> Current stock state.
> 
> Fields:
> - `id`
> - `patient_id`
> - `supply_item_id`
> - `quantity_on_hand`
> - `quantity_reserved`
> - `last_counted_at`
> - `notes`
> 
> ## Add `supply_events`
> Usage/movement log.
> 
> Fields:
> - `id`
> - `patient_id`
> - `supply_item_id`
> - `event_type` (`used`, `opened`, `ordered`, `received`, `discarded`, `corrected`)
> - `quantity_change`
> - `occurred_at`
> - `notes`
> 
> This is how you power “what should we order.”
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 4. Oxygen tank runtime needs estimation, not just counts
> A tank is not like a pill bottle. Runtime depends on:
> - tank type / capacity
> - current pressure or starting state
> - flow rate
> - elapsed time
> 
> ## Add `oxygen_tanks`
> Track actual tanks.
> 
> Fields:
> - `id`
> - `patient_id`
> - `tank_label`
> - `tank_type`
> - `capacity_liters` or `capacity_factor`
> - `current_status` (`full`, `in_use`, `empty`, `returned`, `reserve`)
> - `last_pressure_psi` nullable
> - `last_checked_at`
> - `notes`
> 
> ## Add `oxygen_usage_sessions`
> Track active use.
> 
> Fields:
> - `id`
> - `patient_id`
> - `oxygen_tank_id`
> - `started_at`
> - `ended_at` nullable
> - `flow_rate_lpm`
> - `starting_pressure_psi` nullable
> - `ending_pressure_psi` nullable
> - `estimated_empty_at` nullable
> - `notes`
> 
> This gives you:
> - current estimated depletion time
> - burn rate
> - historical usage pattern
> 
> For forecasting, you can estimate:
> - runtime from tank size + flow rate
> - reorder needs from recent usage trend
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 5. Reordering needs explicit order tables
> You said “hit order list and it knows based on inventory and what’s been taken what we should order.”
> 
> That means we need recommendation + actual order tracking.
> 
> ## Add `supply_orders`
> Fields:
> - `id`
> - `patient_id`
> - `vendor_contact_id`
> - `status`
> - `ordered_at`
> - `expected_at`
> - `received_at`
> - `notes`
> 
> ## Add `supply_order_items`
> Fields:
> - `id`
> - `order_id`
> - `supply_item_id`
> - `quantity_ordered`
> - `quantity_received`
> - `notes`
> 
> Then the worker/AI layer can generate:
> - reorder recommendation list
> - suggested quantities
> - vendor-specific draft order
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 6. CPAP monitoring needs telemetry/history
> You want to catch changes faster.
> 
> That means we need actual device readings, not just “CPAP exists.”
> 
> ## Add `device_profiles`
> For devices like:
> - CPAP
> - concentrator
> - pulse ox
> - nebulizer machine
> 
> Fields:
> - `id`
> - `patient_id`
> - `device_type`
> - `manufacturer`
> - `model`
> - `serial_number`
> - `active`
> - `notes`
> 
> ## Add `device_readings`
> For CPAP/concentrator metrics.
> 
> Fields:
> - `id`
> - `patient_id`
> - `device_profile_id`
> - `reading_type`
> - `reading_name`
> - `reading_value`
> - `reading_unit`
> - `recorded_at`
> - `notes`
> - `metadata_json`
> 
> For CPAP examples:
> - AHI
> - leak rate
> - pressure
> - usage hours
> - humidity setting
> - ramp setting
> 
> This lets you detect:
> - variable changes
> - trend shifts
> - “something changed and symptoms got worse”
>

### User
> give me the prompt to tell this ide step by step, and also i wnat to make a new schema in supabase to put all these tables under it

### Assistant
> I’m checking the current Supabase docs on custom schemas so I don’t hand you outdated setup instructions, then I’ll give you a paste-ready IDE prompt with the exact build sequence.

### Assistant
> Yes — and here’s the clean move.
> 
> ## First, the schema decision
> 
> You **can** create a separate Postgres schema in Supabase for all of this. That is a good idea if you want to keep the care app isolated from `public`. Supabase now supports exposing custom schemas through the Data API, and if you use a custom schema you need to expose it or queries through the API/client will fail. Their docs/troubleshooting also confirm custom schemas can require explicit exposure to the API, and their changelog notes custom schema exposure is now configurable. citeturn787410search5turn787410search6
> 
> My recommendation:
> 
> - create schema: `care`
> - keep app tables under `care.*`
> - leave `public` mostly empty or only for shared utility functions
> - generate types after migrations so frontend and worker share the real DB types. Supabase documents generating types from your database schema. citeturn787410search13
> 
> ## Exact SQL to create the schema first
> 
> Use this in Supabase SQL Editor before the table migrations:
> 
> ```sql
> create schema if not exists care;
> 
> grant usage on schema care to postgres, anon, authenticated, service_role;
> alter default privileges in schema care grant all on tables to postgres, service_role;
> alter default privileges in schema care grant select, insert, update, delete on tables to authenticated;
> alter default privileges in schema care grant usage, select on sequences to authenticated;
> ```
> 
> Then all tables become:
> 
> ```sql
> create table care.patients (...);
> create table care.medications (...);
> ```
> 
> and so on.
> 
> ## Important Supabase note
> 
> After creating the schema, make sure the `care` schema is exposed to the Data API / API settings for your project, otherwise the frontend client may not see those tables properly. That requirement is called out in Supabase guidance around custom schemas and relation visibility / permission issues. citeturn787410search5turn787410search6
> 
> ---
> 
> # Prompt for your IDE
> 
> Paste this into the IDE agent exactly as-is:
> 
> ```text
> We are building a mobile-first care management app with this architecture:
> 
> - Monorepo structure:
>   - apps/frontend = Vite React app
>   - apps/worker = Cloudflare Worker API/AI layer
>   - packages/shared = shared types and domain models
>   - supabase = migrations, seed, config, db functions
> - Database is Supabase Postgres
> - All app tables must live under a custom Postgres schema named `care`
> - Do NOT put app tables in `public`
> - Use TypeScript everywhere
> 
> Your job is to scaffold the project step by step, without skipping foundations.
> 
> STEP 1 — Create repo structure
> Create this folder structure:
> 
> care-app/
>   apps/
>     frontend/
>     worker/
>   packages/
>     shared/
>   supabase/
>     migrations/
>     functions/
>   docs/
>   imports/
>   tests/
> 
> STEP 2 — Frontend app
> Inside apps/frontend:
> - scaffold a Vite React TypeScript app
> - prepare for mobile-first UI
> - create folders:
>   - src/app
>   - src/components
>   - src/features
>   - src/lib
>   - src/state
>   - src/styles
>   - src/types
> 
> STEP 3 — Worker app
> Inside apps/worker:
> - scaffold a Cloudflare Worker TypeScript app
> - create folders:
>   - src/routes
>   - src/services
>   - src/lib
>   - src/types
> - this worker will handle:
>   - AI review endpoints
>   - discharge parsing endpoints
>   - signed upload endpoints
>   - task/reorder recommendation endpoints
> 
> STEP 4 — Shared package
> Inside packages/shared:
> - create a TypeScript package for shared models/types
> - create folders:
>   - src/db
>   - src/ai
>   - src/domain
>   - src/equipment
> - export everything from src/index.ts
> 
> STEP 5 — Supabase setup
> Inside supabase/migrations:
> - create migration files
> - first migration must create schema `care`
> - all app tables must be created as `care.<table_name>`
> - do not create app tables in public schema
> 
> Create migration 0001 for:
> - create extension if needed
> - create schema care
> - grants/default privileges for care schema
> 
> STEP 6 — Create these tables in schema care
> Core:
> - patients
> - medications
> - medication_events
> - vitals
> - observations
> - encounters
> - milestones
> - conditions
> - care_plans
> - care_plan_items
> - discharge_documents
> - discharge_actions
> - attachments
> 
> Timing / adherence:
> - regimens
> - regimen_events
> 
> Supply / oxygen / reorder:
> - supply_items
> - supply_inventory
> - supply_events
> - oxygen_tanks
> - oxygen_usage_sessions
> - supply_orders
> - supply_order_items
> 
> Device monitoring:
> - device_profiles
> - device_readings
> 
> AI:
> - interactions
> - clinician_ai_reviews
> - clinician_ai_findings
> - clinician_ai_evidence
> 
> Support:
> - inventory_log
> - tasks
> - contacts
> 
> STEP 7 — Use these design rules for tables
> For operational tables, include when applicable:
> - id uuid pk default gen_random_uuid()
> - patient_id uuid fk
> - notes text
> - metadata_json jsonb default '{}'::jsonb
> - created_at timestamptz default now()
> - updated_at timestamptz default now()
> - recorded_at or occurred_at when event-based
> - status where useful
> 
> STEP 8 — Relationships to enforce
> - one patient has many of nearly everything
> - medications belong to patient
> - medication_events link to medication and patient
> - encounters link to patient
> - discharge_documents link to encounter and patient
> - discharge_actions link to discharge_documents
> - care_plan_items link to care_plans
> - regimen_events link to regimens
> - oxygen_usage_sessions link to oxygen_tanks
> - supply_order_items link to supply_orders and supply_items
> - device_readings link to device_profiles
> - clinician_ai_findings link to clinician_ai_reviews
> - clinician_ai_evidence link to clinician_ai_findings
> 
> STEP 9 — Critical real-world behaviors to support
> This app must support:
> - “Did I already take that?”
> - “When was my last treatment?”
> - “Is treatment time due now?”
> - “Do I take this with food?”
> - oxygen tank estimated empty time
> - reorder suggestions based on recent usage and stock
> - CPAP/device variable history to detect changes
> - a Today / Now screen with:
>   - current day/time
>   - next med due
>   - last med taken
>   - next treatment due
>   - last treatment completed
>   - oxygen estimate
>   - urgent tasks
> 
> STEP 10 — Generate Mermaid ERD
> Create docs/care_app_erd.mmd using the final table set and relationships.
> 
> STEP 11 — Generate shared DB types
> After migrations are in place, prepare the project to use generated Supabase database types and place them in:
> - packages/shared/src/db/database.types.ts
> 
> STEP 12 — Do not overbuild UI yet
> Only scaffold these feature areas:
> - dashboard
> - events
> - discharge
> - care-plans
> - tasks
> - contacts
> - ai-reviews
> - equipment
> 
> STEP 13 — First screens to implement after scaffold
> 1. Today / Now screen
> 2. Quick Add flow
> 3. Med/treatment adherence log
> 4. Oxygen/supply dashboard
> 5. Discharge action list
> 
> Now scaffold the repo, create the migration plan, and show me the resulting file tree plus the first migration files.
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # What to tell the IDE about the custom Supabase schema specifically
> 
> Add this follow-up prompt right after:
> 
> ```text
> Important Supabase rule:
> - use custom schema `care`
> - all tables must be created under `care`
> - assume we will expose `care` in Supabase API settings
> - all queries from frontend/worker should target schema `care`
> - organize migrations under supabase/migrations using Supabase CLI conventions
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # My blunt recommendation on the schema
> 
> Use **`care`** now. Do not wait.
> 
> Why:
> - cleaner separation
> - easier mental model
> - less junk in `public`
> - better long-term discipline
> 
> Just remember:
> - create the schema
> - expose it to Supabase API settings
> - generate types after migrations. Supabase supports generated types from the actual database schema, which is exactly what you want for the shared package. citeturn787410search13turn787410search5turn787410search6
> 
> If you want, next I’ll give you the **actual first migration files** in order: `0001_create_care_schema.sql`, `0002_core_tables.sql`, `0003_regimens_and_adherence.sql`, etc.

### User
> yes i just ran the first sql you gave me for the care schema.

### Assistant
> Good. That means the foundation is in place.
> 
> Next move is to create the migrations in a sane order so the IDE doesn’t build itself into a corner.
> 
> ## Migration plan
> 
> Use this sequence:
> 
> 1. `0001_create_care_schema.sql`  
> 2. `0002_core_tables.sql`  
> 3. `0003_care_plans_and_discharge.sql`  
> 4. `0004_regimens_and_adherence.sql`  
> 5. `0005_supplies_oxygen_devices.sql`  
> 6. `0006_ai_and_support.sql`  
> 7. `0007_indexes.sql`  
> 
> ---
> 
> # 0001_create_care_schema.sql
> 
> You already ran this manually, but keep it as migration history anyway.
> 
> ```sql
> create extension if not exists pgcrypto;
> 
> create schema if not exists care;
> 
> grant usage on schema care to postgres, anon, authenticated, service_role;
> alter default privileges in schema care grant all on tables to postgres, service_role;
> alter default privileges in schema care grant select, insert, update, delete on tables to authenticated;
> alter default privileges in schema care grant usage, select on sequences to authenticated;
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # 0002_core_tables.sql
> 
> ```sql
> create table care.patients (
>   id uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),
>   full_name text,
>   dob date,
>   baseline_notes text,
>   metadata_json jsonb not null default '{}'::jsonb,
>   created_at timestamptz not null default now(),
>   updated_at timestamptz not null default now()
> );
> 
> create table care.medications (
>   id uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),
>   patient_id uuid not null references care.patients(id) on delete cascade,
>   medication_name text not null,
>   strength text,
>   form text,
>   prescriber text,
>   dosage_instructions text,
>   frequency text,
>   quantity_prescribed numeric,
>   quantity_remaining numeric,
>   active boolean not null default true,
>   notes text,
>   metadata_json jsonb not null default '{}'::jsonb,
>   created_at timestamptz not null default now(),
>   updated_at timestamptz not null default now()
> );
> 
> create table care.encounters (
>   id uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),
>   patient_id uuid not null references care.patients(id) on delete cascade,
>   encounter_type text,
>   provider_name text,
>   facility text,
>   status text,
>   occurred_at timestamptz,
>   summary text,
>   med_changes text,
>   follow_up_needed text,
>   notes text,
>   metadata_json jsonb not null default '{}'::jsonb,
>   created_at timestamptz not null default now(),
>   updated_at timestamptz not null default now()
> );
> 
> create table care.vitals (
>   id uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),
>   patient_id uuid not null references care.patients(id) on delete cascade,
>   encounter_id uuid references care.encounters(id) on delete set null,
>   systolic integer,
>   diastolic integer,
>   pulse integer,
>   oxygen integer,
>   temp numeric,
>   context text,
>   notes text,
>   recorded_at timestamptz not null default now(),
>   metadata_json jsonb not null default '{}'::jsonb
> );
> 
> create table care.observations (
>   id uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),
>   patient_id uuid not null references care.patients(id) on delete cascade,
>   encounter_id uuid references care.encounters(id) on delete set null,
>   category text,
>   subtype text,
>   severity integer,
>   body_area text,
>   notes text,
>   recorded_at timestamptz not null default now(),
>   metadata_json jsonb not null default '{}'::jsonb
> );
> 
> create table care.milestones (
>   id uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),
>   patient_id uuid not null references care.patients(id) on delete cascade,
>   name text not null,
>   metric text,
>   value numeric,
>   baseline_value numeric,
>   target_value numeric,
>   unit text,
>   notes text,
>   recorded_at timestamptz not null default now(),
>   metadata_json jsonb not null default '{}'::jsonb
> );
> 
> create table care.conditions (
>   id uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),
>   patient_id uuid not null references care.patients(id) on delete cascade,
>   category text,
>   summary text,
>   risks text,
>   actions text,
>   status text,
>   metadata_json jsonb not null default '{}'::jsonb,
>   created_at timestamptz not null default now(),
>   updated_at timestamptz not null default now()
> );
> 
> create table care.attachments (
>   id uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),
>   patient_id uuid not null references care.patients(id) on delete cascade,
>   encounter_id uuid references care.encounters(id) on delete set null,
>   file_name text,
>   file_type text,
>   storage_path text,
>   attachment_kind text,
>   notes text,
>   metadata_json jsonb not null default '{}'::jsonb,
>   uploaded_at timestamptz not null default now()
> );
> 
> create table care.medication_events (
>   id uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),
>   patient_id uuid not null references care.patients(id) on delete cascade,
>   medication_id uuid references care.medications(id) on delete set null,
>   encounter_id uuid references care.encounters(id) on delete set null,
>   action text not null,
>   dose_taken text,
>   quantity_change numeric,
>   reason text,
>   notes text,
>   source_type text,
>   occurred_at timestamptz not null default now(),
>   created_at timestamptz not null default now(),
>   metadata_json jsonb not null default '{}'::jsonb
> );
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # 0003_care_plans_and_discharge.sql
> 
> ```sql
> create table care.care_plans (
>   id uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),
>   patient_id uuid not null references care.patients(id) on delete cascade,
>   title text not null,
>   status text,
>   start_date date,
>   end_date date,
>   created_by text,
>   source_type text,
>   summary text,
>   precautions text,
>   escalation_rules text,
>   notes text,
>   metadata_json jsonb not null default '{}'::jsonb,
>   created_at timestamptz not null default now(),
>   updated_at timestamptz not null default now()
> );
> 
> create table care.care_plan_items (
>   id uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),
>   care_plan_id uuid not null references care.care_plans(id) on delete cascade,
>   patient_id uuid not null references care.patients(id) on delete cascade,
>   category text,
>   item_text text not null,
>   frequency text,
>   status text,
>   target_metric text,
>   target_value numeric,
>   notes text,
>   metadata_json jsonb not null default '{}'::jsonb,
>   created_at timestamptz not null default now(),
>   updated_at timestamptz not null default now()
> );
> 
> alter table care.observations
>   add column care_plan_id uuid references care.care_plans(id) on delete set null;
> 
> alter table care.milestones
>   add column care_plan_id uuid references care.care_plans(id) on delete set null;
> 
> create table care.discharge_documents (
>   id uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),
>   patient_id uuid not null references care.patients(id) on delete cascade,
>   encounter_id uuid references care.encounters(id) on delete set null,
>   document_title text,
>   discharge_date date,
>   facility text,
>   provider_name text,
>   summary text,
>   medication_changes_text text,
>   follow_up_text text,
>   warning_signs_text text,
>   raw_text text,
>   status text,
>   metadata_json jsonb not null default '{}'::jsonb,
>   created_at timestamptz not null default now(),
>   updated_at timestamptz not null default now()
> );
> 
> create table care.discharge_actions (
>   id uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),
>   patient_id uuid not null references care.patients(id) on delete cascade,
>   discharge_document_id uuid not null references care.discharge_documents(id) on delete cascade,
>   action_type text,
>   action_text text not null,
>   due_date date,
>   status text,
>   completed_at timestamptz,
>   notes text,
>   metadata_json jsonb not null default '{}'::jsonb,
>   created_at timestamptz not null default now(),
>   updated_at timestamptz not null default now()
> );
> 
> alter table care.attachments
>   add column discharge_document_id uuid references care.discharge_documents(id) on delete set null,
>   add column care_plan_id uuid references care.care_plans(id) on delete set null;
> 
> alter table care.medication_events
>   add column discharge_document_id uuid references care.discharge_documents(id) on delete set null;
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> # 0004_regimens_and_adherence.sql
> 
> This is the big “did I take it / is it due” layer.
> 
> ```sql
> create table care.regimens (
>   id uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),
>   patient_id uuid not null references care.patients(id) on delete cascade,
>   regimen_type text not null,
>   title text not null,
>   linked_medication_id uuid references care.medications(id) on delete set null,
>   instructions text,
>   with_food boolean,
>   food_instruction_text text,
>   is_prn boolean not null default false,
>   min_interval_minutes integer,
>   schedule_type text not null,
>   schedule_json jsonb not null default '{}'::jsonb,
>   active boolean not null default true,
>   metadata_json jsonb not null default '{}'::jsonb,
>   created_at timestamptz not null default now(),
>   updated_at timestamptz not null default now()
> );
> 
> create table care.regimen_events (
>   id uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),
>   patient_id uuid not null references care.patients(id) on delete cascade,
>   regimen_id uuid not null references care.regimens(id) on delete cascade,
>   status text not null,
>   performed_at timestamptz not null default now(),
>   notes text,
>   source_type text,
>   metadata_json jsonb not null default '{}'::jsonb
> );
> ```
>
